  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1771200876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1771200876" />
    <a title="Raquel Baggins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60099374-raquel-baggins"><img alt="Raquel Baggins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601211766p2/60099374.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1771200876?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Raquel Baggins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Raquel Baggins" href="/user/show/60099374-raquel-baggins">Raquel Baggins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788483839492" href="/book/show/23199295-underground">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60099374-raquel-baggins?shelf=asian-lit">asian-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60099374-raquel-baggins?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60099374-raquel-baggins?shelf=haruki-murakami">haruki-murakami</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1771200876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer341366331200695217"><b>3.5 ★★★</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>«The rain that fell on the city runs down the dark gutters and empties into the sea without even soaking the ground»</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>Review in English | Reseña en español (abajo)</b><br/><br/>I had this book on my tbr for more than four years but I never dared to read it. The main reasons: I didn’t like the two non-fiction books I've read written by Haruki Murakami –<i> What I Talk About When I Talk About Running</i> and <i>What I Talk About When I Talk About Writing</i>–, and I thought that the 'essayist’ Murakami wasn’t my cup</span>
  <span id="freeText341366331200695217" style="display:none"><b>3.5 ★★★</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>«The rain that fell on the city runs down the dark gutters and empties into the sea without even soaking the ground»</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Review in English | Reseña en español (abajo)</b><br /><br />I had this book on my tbr for more than four years but I never dared to read it. The main reasons: I didn’t like the two non-fiction books I've read written by Haruki Murakami –<i> What I Talk About When I Talk About Running</i> and <i>What I Talk About When I Talk About Writing</i>–, and I thought that the 'essayist’ Murakami wasn’t my cup of tea; the theme and synopsis scared me: this book is a work of interviews to the victims of the sarin gas attack in the Tokyo subway in 1995; the considerable size of the book (almost 600 pages); and my disappointment with the last novel I read by Murakami a few months ago: 1Q84. Even so, I wanted to give it an opportunity and so have no bad conscience to continue buying and reading Murakami's books (he’s my absolutely favourite author).<br /><br /><i>Underground</i> is not an easy or light reading and, in my case, it has nothing to do with what I’ve read in my whole life. Underground is a research, documentation and interview work with which Murakami wanted to answer a question: <i>what is the Japanese psyche like?</i> (when faced with tragedies like the one that happened on the morning of March 20, 1995 in Tokyo). It is a subject that, although it may seem very distant (in time and space), unfortunately it is of a certain relevance and remains similar to us (due to the human condition that allows us to empathize, also to the different terrorist attacks that we live near or see through the news...). And, in addition, in this case it is a subject that causes us discomfort: we could’ve been victims and we understand their pain (I was especially moved and broken with Shizuko Akashi’s story), but we also come to understand that <i>place that they promised</i> to all the people linked to the Buddhist sect Aum Shinrikyo.<br /><br />However, I must admit that the final part of the interviews with the victims of the attack came to overwhelm me a lot, and the book structure that is noted at the beginning begins to be disorganised (in total there are around 70 interviews of at least 6 pages, and the format is not easy to read). I must say that I especially liked the inclusion in this edition of the <i>Post-Underground</i> interviews that Murakami had with members and ex-members of the Aum sect and that were originally published in the Japanese magazine <i>Bungei Shunju</i> after the release of the book in Japan.<br /><br />In short, I think it is a necessary book regardless of whether you like Murakami's narrative or not, and that doesn't leave anyone indifferent. It is a hard story but one that makes you want to continue investigating what happened and about the problems of religious sects and terrorist attacks. Highly recommended to read it little by little.<br /><br /><b>P. S. I'm not English, so if you see any mistakes let me know so I can correct them, please</b><br />—<br />Tenía este libro en mi estantería desde hacía más de cuatro años y nunca me animaba a leerlo. Las razones: los dos libros que he leído de no ficción escritos por Haruki Murakami –<i>De qué hablo cuando hablo de correr</i> y <i>De qué hablo cuando hablo de escribir</i>– no me han llegado a gustar y creía que el Murakami más 'ensayista' no me aportaba demasiado; la temática y sinopsis me asustaba: este libro es un trabajo de entrevistas a algunas de las víctimas del atentado de gas sarín en el metro de Tokio en 1995; el tamaño considerable del libro (casi unas 600 páginas); y mi decepción con la última novela que leí del autor hace unos meses: 1Q84. Aun así, quise darle (al fin) una oportunidad a este libro y así no tener mala conciencia para seguir comprando y leyendo los libros del autor japonés.<br /><br /><i>Underground</i> no es una lectura fácil ni ligera y, en mi caso, no tiene nada que ver con lo que haya leído en toda mi vida. Underground es un trabajo de investigación, documentación y entrevistas con el que Murakami quería responder a una pregunta: <i>¿cómo es la psique japonesa?</i> (cuando debe enfrentarse a tragedias como la que sucedió la mañana del 20 de marzo de 1995 en Tokio). Es un tema que, aunque nos pueda llegar a parecer muy lejano (en el tiempo y en el espacio), desgraciadamente es de cierta actualidad y nos queda igualmente cercano (por la propia condición humana que nos permite empatizar, por los diferentes ataques terroristas que vivimos cerca o vemos a través de las noticias…). Y, además, en este caso es un tema que nos produce cierta irritación: podríamos haber sido víctimas y comprendemos su dolor (me quedé especialmente conmovida y rota con la historia de Shizuko Akashi), pero también llegamos a comprender ese <i>lugar que prometieron</i> a las personas vinculadas con la secta budista Aum Shinrikyo.<br /><br />Con todo, debo admitir que la parte final de las entrevistas a las víctimas del atentado llegaron a abrumarme bastante, y la organización que se nota al principio del libro comienza a ser más laxa (en total son en torno a 70 entrevistas de mínimo 6 páginas, y el formato es complicado para leer de una sentada). Debo decir que me gustó especialmente la inclusión en esta edición de las entrevistas <i>Post-Underground</i> que Murakami mantuvo con miembros y ex-miembros de la secta Aum y que fueron originalmente publicadas en la revista <i>Bungei Shunju</i> tras la publicación del libro en Japón.<br /><br />En definitiva, creo que es un libro necesario independientemente de si te gusta la narrativa de Murakami o no, y que no deja indiferente a nadie. Es una historia dura pero que te hace querer seguir indagando sobre lo sucedido y sobre la problemática de las sectas religiosas y ataques terroristas. Muy recomendable para leer poquito a poco.</span>
  <a data-text-id="341366331200695217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iK8n+bL9EX38bdewnGNFJ70QvW1MWKyzoIEPGcj//0PSP1eOkBkUEuJupZLv3EjltlqZ6siJHaG9Px1n7nQGNQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('P6q40PXdDh+uYpbESQEA1QWLbZUWwuqTkPiHUlv6a2plOsin1zkLcLBh5OY6vg0XDsFJEpITW4GNRpUsfXGSHA==')})
  }

Finally in this book readers will find a map to the strange realm that grounds virtually every aspect of Murakami’s writing. A journey through the enigmatic and baffling innermost mind, a metaphysical dimension where Murakami’s most bizarre scenes and characters lurk, The Forbidden Worlds of Haruki Murakami exposes the psychological and mythological underpinnings of this other world. Matthew Carl Strecher shows how these considerations color Murakami’s depictions of the individual and collective soul, which constantly shift between the tangible and intangible but in this literary landscape are undeniably real.\n\nThrough these otherworldly depths The Forbidden Worlds of Haruki Murakami also charts the writer’s vivid “inner world,” whether unconscious or underworld (what some Japanese critics call achiragawa, or “over there”), and its connectivity to language. Strecher covers all of Murakami’s work—including his efforts as a literary journalist—and concludes with the first full-length close reading of the writer’s newest novel, Colorless Tsukuru Tazaki and Müellifin kendisi bu iki hususu risalelerinde belirtmiştir. Risale-i Nur, konuları ele alış tarzı, muhtevasındaki derinliği ve kapsamlılığı birçok kesimin yoğun ilgisini çekmiştir. Bir yandan yurt içinde ve dışında çeşitli halk kesimleri tarafından okunmakta ve diğer yandan hakkında uluslararası sempozyumlar düzenlenmekte ve birçok akademik makale ve tezlere konu olmaktadır. Mesela bunlar arasında çağdaş düşünürlerden Faslı Prof. Dr. Taha Abdurrahman, Risale-i Nur\'un düşünce dünyasında yaptığı büyük devrimden söz ederken, onun diğer yönlerinin yanında bu yönünün de kayda değer olduğuna dikkat çekmektedir: &quot;Bazı Batılı filozoflar, her şeyin merkezine aklı aldılar ve sadece aklın ürünü olan hususlara itibar ettiler. Hatta bu hususta öyle ileri gittiler ki, İncil ve Kur\'an gibi semavi kitapları ve temsil ettikleri dinleri de aklın etrafında dönen diğer eşya arasına katarak, akli sistem içinde onlara bir tanım getirdiler. Yani, tıpkı eski insanların dünyayı sabit sanıp güneşin de onun etrafında döndüğünü tevehhüm ettikleri gibi, aklı sabit kabul ederek semavi kitap ve dinleri onun etrafında gezdirdiler. &quot;İşte Bediüzzaman, Risale-i Nur\'la düşünce dünyasındaki bu gidişatı olması gereken mecraya çevirdi, tıpkı ilim dünyasında Kopernik\'in yaptığı gibi. Nasıl ki Kopernik, \'Dünyanın sabit, güneşin onun etrafında döndüğü şeklindeki eski görüşü ortadan kaldırıp; onun yerine, dünyanın hem kendi etrafında, hem güneşin etrafında döndüğünü\' ispat etti; Bediüzzaman da Risale-i Nur\'la düşünce dünyasında buna benzer bir inkılap gerçekleştirdi: \'İnsanın düşünce dünyası sabit olamaz. Düşünce dünyası hem kendi ekseni etrafında döner, hem de vahiy güneşinin etrafında döner\' diyerek insan düşüncesinin olması gereken asıl yerini tespit etmiş, aklı yalnızlık ve karanlıktan kurtararak aydınlatmış ve rahatlatmıştır.&quot; Ayrıca Risale-i Nur, bir Kur\'an tefsiri olması itibariyle, aklın yanı sıra, kalb, ruh ve diğer bütün duygulara da hitap etmektedir. Ahlakın bütün boyutlarına ışık tutmakta ve bir çok sosyal probleme çözümler sunmaktadır. Ancak onun bu ve benzeri daha bir çok meziyetini en iyi şekilde anlamanın yolu her halde onu açıp bizatihi okumak ve yaşamakla olur.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3354.Haruki_Murakami">About Haruki Murakami</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3354.Haruki_Murakami"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1539035376p3/3354.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3354.Haruki_Murakami">Haruki Murakami
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
82,911
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8832640979012313069"><b>Murakami</b> Haruki (Japanese: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11882216' rel='nofollow noopener'>村上 春樹</a>) is a popular contemporary Japanese writer and translator. His work has been described as <i>'easily accessible, yet profoundly complex'</i>. He can be located on Facebook at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.facebook.com/harukimurakamiauthor'>https://www.facebook.com/harukimuraka...</a><br/><br/>Since childhood, Murakami has been heavily influenced by Western culture, particularly Western music and literature. He grew up reading a range of works by Am</span>
  <span id="freeText8832640979012313069" style="display:none"><b>Murakami</b> Haruki (Japanese: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11882216" rel="nofollow noopener">村上 春樹</a>) is a popular contemporary Japanese writer and translator. His work has been described as <i>'easily accessible, yet profoundly complex'</i>. He can be located on Facebook at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/harukimurakamiauthor">https://www.facebook.com/harukimuraka...</a><br /><br />Since childhood, Murakami has been heavily influenced by Western culture, particularly Western music and literature. He grew up reading a range of works by American writers, such as Kurt Vonnegut and Richard Brautigan, and he is often distinguished from other Japanese writers by his Western influences.<br /><br />Murakami studied drama at Waseda University in Tokyo, where he met his wife, Yoko. His first job was at a record store, which is where one of his main characters, Toru Watanabe in <i>Norwegian Wood</i>, works. Shortly before finishing his studies, Murakami opened the coffeehouse <i>'Peter Cat'</i> which was a jazz bar in the evening in Kokubunji, Tokyo with his wife.<br /><br />Many of his novels have themes and titles that invoke classical music, such as the three books making up <i>The Wind-Up Bird Chronicle</i>: <i>The Thieving Magpie</i> (after Rossini's opera), <i>Bird as Prophet</i> (after a piano piece by Robert Schumann usually known in English as <i>The Prophet Bird</i>), and <i>The Bird-Catcher</i> (a character in Mozart's opera <i>The Magic Flute</i>). Some of his novels take their titles from songs: <i>Dance, Dance, Dance</i> (after The Dells' song, although it is widely thought it was titled after the <i>Beach Boys</i> tune), <i>Norwegian Wood</i> (after The Beatles' song) and <i>South of the Border, West of the Sun</i> (the first part being the title of a song by Nat King Cole).<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8832640979012313069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/6179816">Quotes from Underground</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;If you lose your ego, you lose the thread of that narrative you call your Self. Humans, however, can't live very long without some sense of a continuing story. Such stories go beyond the limited rational system (or the systematic rationality) with which you surround yourself; they are crucial keys to sharing time-experience with others. <br /><br />Now a narrative is a story, not a logic, nor ethics, nor philosophy. It is a dream you keep having, whether you realize it or not. Just as surely as you breathe, you go on ceaselessly dreaming your story. And in these stories you wear two faces. You are simultaneously subject and object. You are a whole and you are a part. You are real and you are shadow. "Storyteller" and at the same time "character". It is through such multilayering of roles in our stories that we heal the loneliness of being an isolated individual in the world. <br /><br />Yet without a proper ego nobody can create a personal narrative, any more than you can drive a car without an engine, or cast a shadow without a real physical object. But once you've consigned your ego to someone else, where on earth do you go from there?<br /><br />At this point you receive a new narrative from the person to whom you have entrusted your ego. You've handed over the real thing, so what comes back is a shadow. And once your ego has merged with another ego, your narrative will necessarily take on the narrative created by that ego.<br /><br />Just what kind of narrative?<br /><br />It needn't be anything particularly fancy, nothing complicated or refined. You don't need to have literary ambitions. In fact, the sketchier and simpler the better. Junk, a leftover rehash will do. Anyway, most people are tired of complex, multilayered scenarios-they are a potential letdown. It's precisely because people can't find any fixed point within their own multilayered schemes that they're tossing aside their own self-identity.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/518548-if-you-lose-your-ego-you-lose-the-thread-of">30 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;The rain that fell on the city runs down the dark gutters and empties into the sea without even soaking the ground&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/639379-the-rain-that-fell-on-the-city-runs-down-the">25 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/6179816">More quotes&hellip;</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
